## §4. Formal F-flag registry + marker convention

This section records the five formally-promoted F-flags (F129, F130, F131, F132, F137) with operational definitions + sibling/parent relationships; brief F138 reference (informal-discipline; promotion candidate); the archived VR §265 `# APPROXIMATION:` + `# SCAFFOLDING:` enumeration convention; and a cross-reference note to F-flag candidates tracked at informal-discipline scope.

### §4.1 Operational scope and discipline structure

F-flags are **audit-machinery patterns** that identify systematic failure modes at derivation and verification work. Each formally-promoted F-flag carries:

- **Operational definition** — what the failure mode is, what it flags.
- **Trigger conditions** — when an audit applies the flag.
- **Required discipline** — what derivation work must do to be admissible at canonical-grounding scope (i.e., not flagged).
- **Sibling/parent relationships** — how the flag relates to other formal flags.

F-flag formal status is established by Charles tier-gated authorization at cumulative-precedent threshold (typically two precedents; three for some informal-discipline promotions). Once formal, the flag's discipline carries forward as standing operational rule across sessions.

F-flag candidates (informal-discipline; single-precedent or pending tier-gate) are tracked at archived VR; cross-reference only at §4.10 below.

### §4.2 F129 — Algebraic-consistency-mistaken-for-pinning (parent failure mode)

**Operational definition.** Algebraic consistency of a derivation result with a leading-order prediction is misread as canonical pinning of the result. Dimensional equality without representation isomorphism = algebraic consistency, NOT pinning. The pattern operates at multiple structural layers; F129 is the **parent failure mode** under which more specific flags (F132 at composite-extraction layer; F138 at surface-citation layer) operate.

**Trigger conditions.** A derivation chain that:
- Reproduces a leading-order target numerical value, AND
- Is claimed to be canonically pinned by UDT content, BUT
- Carries approximations or imported scaffolding (per §4.9 marker convention) that are not explicitly enumerated AND error-bounded / canonically-replaced.

**Required discipline.** F129-strict-canonical pinning claims require both `# APPROXIMATION:` and `# SCAFFOLDING:` enumeration blocks to be empty (or all sub-leading drops carry explicit error bounds AND all scaffolding is replaced by canonical-derived equivalents). Otherwise the claim level is canonical-with-approximations, canonical-with-scaffolding, or HYPOTHESIS-grade.

**Scope.** Multi-application; active across all derivation work targeting canonical-content claims.

### §4.3 F130 — Continuum-momentum-space scaffolding (content-side import flag)

**Operational definition.** Flags derivations that invoke flat-space continuum-momentum-space machinery applied locally to UDT cavity content. Specific imports flagged:

- Full 3D phase-space DOS formula $\rho_{3D}^{\rm flat}(E) = k^2 \cdot dk/dE / (2\pi^2)$
- Unbounded κ-sum at curved-cavity scope
- Classical-turning-point cutoff $\kappa_{\max}(r, E) = E \cdot r \cdot e^{+2\phi}$

These are flat-space constructions; not derived from canonical UDT content. F130 is **formally promoted** at two-precedent threshold.

**Trigger conditions.** Any derivation chain on UDT canonical content that imports one or more of the above continuum-momentum-space objects without canonical-content derivation from UDT metric / Form-T / cavity structure.

**Required discipline.** Flag as `# SCAFFOLDING:` per §4.9 marker convention. Promotion to canonical pinning requires either (a) replacement by canonical-derived equivalent (first-principles UDT 3D DOS derivation), or (b) explicit canonical justification at full-3D scope. **Scaffolding work cannot land as F129-pinned at strict canonical level** until replaced.

**Sibling flags.** F131 (method-class vigilance, methodology-side companion); F132 (composite-extraction failure mode, content-side companion).

### §4.4 F131 — Method-class vigilance for flat-space-DOS-reproduction methods (method-side import flag)

**Operational definition.** Flags derivation **methods** whose structural shape reproduces flat-space behavior at zero-curvature limit. Specific method classes flagged:

- Path-integral M1
- Heat-kernel / Seeley-DeWitt M2
- Spectral zeta M2-extension
- Atiyah-Singer / AHS construction
- Variational M1-variants

Leading-order output coincidence with imported scaffolding (e.g., $a_0 = 1$ free-heat-kernel term) is locally-flat reproduction, **not canonical-content validation**. This is the F129 failure mode in **method form** — agreement at flat-space limit does not establish canonical pinning at curved cavity scope.

**Trigger conditions.** A derivation method chartered for first-principles work that produces output indistinguishable from flat-space limit at leading order; method's structural shape (not just output value) reproduces imported scaffolding's free term.

**Required discipline.** Methods in this class chartered for canonical-content work must produce output **beyond leading-order zero-curvature limit** before canonical pinning claims. Method-selection at charter design should prefer methods that do NOT reproduce flat-space DOS at leading order (e.g., canonical mode-counting on Pell-fixed κ-orbit at canonical (1/2, 1, 3) triple per §1.7).

**Sibling flags.** F130 (content-side companion at scaffolding-import-flag layer); F132 (content-side composite-extraction layer).

### §4.5 F132 — Fit-window-geometric-coupling-dominance at φ-exponent extraction (content-side, S61)

**Operational definition.** Flags derivations that extract a φ-exponent target value via log ρ-vs-φ fit at a chosen fit-window. The extracted exponent decomposes structurally as:

$$\beta_{\rm fit} \;=\; \alpha_{\rm canonical} \;+\; \frac{d(-n \log r)}{d\phi}\bigg|_{\rm fit-window}$$

When the geometric coupling slope (second term) dominates the numerical value, measured β is **not the canonical-content quantity** — α is. Treating β as canonical pinning is F129 at composite level.

F132 is **formally promoted** at two-precedent threshold.

**Trigger conditions.** A PONDER §-header or canonical-grounding claim that:
- Targets a numerical β value as "profile-universal canonical content," AND
- Does not enumerate the structural decomposition above, OR
- Verifies Rule 19 universality at β-layer rather than α-layer (see F137).

**Required discipline.** Every φ-exponent extraction PONDER §-header must declare canonical-α (profile-universal) vs composite-β (profile-specific) target AND enumerate the structural decomposition explicitly at canonical-grounding scope. Profile-universality verification (Rule 19) must target α-layer when both α and β are accessible from the same canonical quantity.

**Sibling flags.** F137 (methodology-side companion at Rule 19 verification layer); child of F129 parent.

**Cross-reference.** §2.2 above (canonical β decomposition for α = +2 baseline).

### §4.6 F137 — α-layer Rule 19 verification cleaner than β-layer (methodology-side, S61)

**Operational definition.** Rule 19 universality verification at α-layer is structurally **cleaner** than at β-layer at the same precision when both α and β are accessible from the same canonical quantity. β-layer verification fails substantively when profile-specific geometric coupling slope dominates **despite** canonical-content profile-universality of α. Distinct verification outcomes at the two layers indicate this failure mode.

F137 is **formally promoted** at two-precedent threshold.

**Trigger conditions.** Rule 19 universality test that:
- Targets β-layer when α-layer is also accessible from same canonical quantity, AND
- Yields negative universality verdict at β-layer that does NOT propagate to α-layer.

**Required discipline.** Apply F132 structural decomposition first; then test Rule 19 universality at α-layer. β-layer R19 fails when geometric coupling dominates; α-layer R19 confirms profile-universality of canonical content (when present). Treat β-layer R19 as geometric-coupling-stability test across profiles, **not as canonical-content profile-universality test**.

**Sibling flags.** F132 (content-side companion). Together F132 + F137 form the **content + methodology vigilance pair** at φ-exponent extraction and verification.

**Cross-reference.** §2.3 above (α = +2 R19 universality verification status).

### §4.7 F138 — Surface-fidelity-vs-document-genre (informal-discipline; promotion candidate)

**Operational definition.** Flags label-vs-content mismatches at canonical-record entries: when a label, status banner, or surface citation does not accurately reflect the canonical content of the entry. Examples surfaced at archived VR §263.5 catalog: status label "DERIVED" applied to a PARTIALLY-DERIVED-WITH-OPEN-GROUNDING entry; "BC exact" applied to BC-broken-with-residual canonical content; canonical-formula label divergence at sibling sections (e.g., §8.5.4 vs §8.5.5 "source" labels with different κGF cross-term content).

**Status (at S63 close).** Informal-discipline; cumulative confirming-instance count at **+5** (catalog F138-1 through F138-5 at archived VR §263.5). **Promotion candidate at later session** per VR §263.5 catalog convention if additional precedents accrue.

**Trigger conditions.** Audit reads a canonical-record label or status banner; canonical content of the entry does not match the surface fidelity of the label.

**Required discipline (informal).** Label-corrections + canonical-content-clarifications applied at audit catch. Operational at audit-of-canonical-record-edits scope; not yet formally part of the F-flag operative-rule family.

**Sibling/parent.** Child of F129 parent (surface-citation layer; sibling to F132 composite-extraction layer).

**Cross-reference.** Full F138-1 through F138-5 catalog at archived VR §263.5 (not duplicated here per anti-pull AP6 informal-discipline tracking).

### §4.8 Sibling/parent relationships

```
                    F129 (parent)
                  Algebraic-consistency
                  mistaken-for-pinning
                  /          |          \
                 /           |           \
          F132              F138         (F130 / F131 import-flag pair
   Composite-extraction   Surface-citation  operates at scaffolding-import
   layer                   layer            layer; F129 parentage)
   (content side)           (informal;
   (Rule 19 partner:        promotion
    F137)                    candidate)
```

**Pair structure:**

- **F132 + F137 = content + methodology vigilance pair at φ-exponent extraction and verification.** F132 catches when β is misread as canonical content (content side); F137 catches when R19 is mis-targeted at β-layer instead of α-layer (methodology side).
- **F130 + F131 = content-side + method-class scaffolding-import pair.** F130 catches when the content imported is flat-space DOS / κ-sum / κ-cutoff (object-side); F131 catches when the derivation method's structural shape reproduces such imports (method-side).
- **F138 = surface-citation layer of F129 parent**; informal-discipline tracking, promotion candidate at +5 cumulative.

### §4.9 Archived VR §265 marker convention

Operational standing rule from S60-004 (archived VR §265). Derivation scripts and PONDER §-headers enumerate approximations + imported machinery explicitly at landing.

#### §4.9.1 `# APPROXIMATION:` marker

Flags controlled approximation steps. Examples:

- WKB leading-order (state sub-leading drops; explicit at §2 above for α = +2)
- Linearization in small parameters
- Continuum treatment of discrete sums
- Mode-averaging over oscillations

**Requirement.** Explicitly state regime of validity AND error-bound status. Work without explicit error bounds is flagged as `# APPROXIMATION (no error bound established):`.

#### §4.9.2 `# SCAFFOLDING:` marker

Flags imported machinery from another paradigm. Examples:

- Flat-space DOS formulas applied locally to curved metrics (F130 territory)
- Gauge-fixing conventions imported from other sectors
- Renormalization schemes (Anderson-Hiscock-Samuel, etc.)
- Numerical methods (BVP solvers, integration schemes)
- Boundary-condition conventions imported from non-UDT contexts

**Requirement.** Explicitly identify source paradigm AND promotion path to canonical replacement. **Scaffolding work cannot land as "F129-pinned at strict canonical level"** until replaced by canonical-derived equivalent.

#### §4.9.3 PONDER §-header requirement

Derivations citing chain elements as "forced by canonical content" must include the following enumeration block at §-header:

```
## Approximations + scaffolding enumeration

**Approximations:** (none) OR (list each with regime + error-bound status)
**Scaffolding:** (none) OR (list each with source + promotion path)
**F129 pinning claim level:** [strict canonical / canonical-with-approximations / canonical-with-scaffolding / HYPOTHESIS-grade]
```

**F129-strict-canonical claims require both enumeration blocks empty** (or all sub-leading drops carry explicit error bounds AND all scaffolding canonically replaced).

#### §4.9.4 Audit machinery

Audit machinery interrogates enumeration blocks at each landing. **Absence of enumeration block is a flag, not default-acceptable.**

### §4.10 F-flag candidates (informal-discipline; cross-reference only)

Several F-flag candidates are tracked at informal-discipline scope (single-precedent or multi-precedent pending Charles tier-gate authorization). Catalog stays at archived VR per AP6 informal-discipline tracking.

FIVE GATING ITEMS POST-S95; THREE-OBSERVABLE CLOSURE PRESERVED; 2026-05-25 evening):** Cumulative S95 substantive arc produced complete theory → verifier → empirical chain at framework's polarization-phase observable. **S95-001 PONDER:** factor-91 reconciliation at framework §12.6 Step 5 reveals RECONCILIATION-DISSOLVES-VIA-REFRAMING-AT-CANONICAL-CONTENT-LAYER-IDENTIFICATION-AMBIGUITY; spin-2 Fourier suppression scale $w$ (operator-derived) and hydrostatic scale height $H$ (layer-specific) are structurally distinct length scales; layer-identification at canonical content is OPEN gating item. **S95-002 PONDER:** TT-EE phase-shift derivation tightening reveals PHASE-SHIFT-DOES-NOT-CLOSE-AT-CANONICAL-CONTENT-STRUCTURAL-FINDING-AT-FRAMEWORK-§12.7; ## §6. Predictive scorecard + standing prohibitions

> **⚠ Status note (2026-05-15, post-S67-005 wind-down):** §6.2 standing prohibitions block below contains references to IH §49.10 §5.11 canonical-content extension territory as **"singular substantive forward direction within composite-matter Phase 2 scope"** (S66-004 framing) at §6.2.5 line 966. This framing is **SUPERSEDED** by IH §49.10 §5.11 revised label "STRUCTURALLY EXHAUSTED AT S67-001" (S67-003 + S67-005 canonical-record-edits) per S67-001 reconnaissance NOT-ADMISSIBLE × 3 + S67-002 §241-BASIS-INTACT dual-support reinforcement. Cross-reference: IH §49.10 §5.11 revised label + IH §49.10 §5.10 forward-arc disposition (post-S67-005). The §6.2.5 prose below preserves the S66-004 historical framing; current state is at §5.11.

This section records (a) the predictive scorecard with canonical-home cross-references to CG, and (b) the standing prohibitions block that defines what derivation and verification work must not do. Canonical derivations live at CG; this section is consolidation / discipline reference, not duplication.

### §6.1 Predictive scorecard

#### §6.1.1 Operational scope

The scorecard records what UDT predicts at the particle-mass level and which formulas have current canonical-derivation status DERIVED vs PARTIALLY-DERIVED-WITH-OPEN-GROUNDING. Canonical derivation chains live at CG (§13 lepton mass derivations + §26.5 cluster framework + §22.5 + §26.5 item 2 open items). This sub-section cross-references; CG is authoritative.

#### §6.1.2 Particle mass formula table

| Particle | UDT formula | PDG relative error | Status | Canonical home |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| Pion $\pi^\pm$ | $m_\pi = 84\pi \cdot m_e$ | **−0.094%** | PARTIALLY-DERIVED-WITH-OPEN-GROUNDING | CG §13.10 |
| Muon $\mu^\pm$ | $m_\mu = (20\pi^3/3) \cdot m_e$ | **−0.029%** | DERIVED | CG §13.3–§13.7 |
| Proton $p$ | $m_p = 6\pi^5 \cdot m_e$ | **−0.002%** | DERIVED | CG §13.3–§13.7 |

Free parameters: zero. The single empirical input is the electron mass $m_e$ (canonical Branch-M anchor at §1.3); all three particle masses follow as algebraic predictions.

Cluster framework: **V2 + V4 + V7** (operative for derived content; V4-origin OPEN at §3.5 / CG §26.5 item 2). Canonical home: CG §26.5.

#### §6.1.3 Sub-formula derivation status

**Lepton sub-formulas — DERIVED.** Muon $20\pi^3/3$ and proton $6\pi^5$ are canonically derived at CG §13.3–§13.7 via the rank-1 $\hat{r}$ angular coupling on $S^2$ + selection rule on the canonical Form-T Dirac (§4.4). The derivation chain is closed at CG canonical-record; PDG agreement at $-0.029\%$ (muon) and $-0.002\%$ (proton) is downstream of the canonical content, not a fit.

**Pion sub-formula — PARTIALLY-DERIVED-WITH-OPEN-GROUNDING.** The coefficient $84$ of $\pi$ in $m_\pi = 84\pi \cdot m_e$ has structural localization at the κ=0 boundary bridge per archived VR §256 + §263. Combinatorial closure (the Diophantine identity $84 = \binom{9}{3} = \dim \operatorname{Sym}^3(\mathbb{R}^7)$ at the Pell triple $(j, \ell, |\kappa_{\max}|) = (1/2, 1, 3)$) is canonical at §1.7. But the **mechanism origin** of the coefficient $84$ (why the Diophantine identity holds geometrically) and the **per-particle π-exponent pattern** (why pion gets $\pi^1$ while muon gets $\pi^3$ and proton gets $\pi^5$) remain OPEN-WITH-STRUCTURAL-LOCALIZATION at the κ=0 boundary — tracked as **D-PION-COEFF + D-PI-POWER-ORIGIN + V4-origin** at §3.5.

F138-1 correction (S59-006): the CG §13.10 status label was earlier "DERIVED"; corrected to PARTIALLY-DERIVED-WITH-OPEN-GROUNDING at audit (informal-discipline F138 surface-fidelity-vs-document-genre catch; see §4.7 + archived VR §263.5 catalog).

**Standing discipline (from SESSION64_PROMPT, see §6.2 below):** do **not** charter directly against the parked sub-questions at §3.5. Closure via side-effect of substantive derivation work permitted.

#### §6.1.4 V2 + V4 + V7 cluster framework

Three components of the translation-operator cluster at canonical home **CG §26.5**:

- **V2** — operative for derived content (lepton sub-formula structure).
- **V4** — origin OPEN at §3.5 (V4-origin canonical mechanism not yet derived); CG §26.5 item 2 is the canonical-record entry for the open question.
- **V7** — operative for derived content (closure-orbit structure at κ=0 boundary cluster).

Cluster framework is canonically operative; **V4-origin** is one of the three κ=0 boundary cluster items at §3.5 (alongside D-PION-COEFF + D-PI-POWER-ORIGIN). Per §6.1.3 standing discipline: closure via side-effect permitted; do not charter directly.

Cross-references: CG §26.5 (cluster framework canonical home); CG §26.5 item 2 (V4-origin canonical-record entry); §3.5 (κ=0 boundary cluster D-items).

#### §6.1.5 Pell triple substrate (cross-reference)

The pion coefficient combinatorial closure ($84 = \binom{9}{3}$) rests on the Pell-DERIVED canonical triple

$$(j,\, \ell,\, |\kappa_{\max}|) = (1/2,\, 1,\, 3)$$

from the fundamental Pell solution $(17, 2)$ of $x^2 - 72 y^2 = 1$ under $x = 4|\kappa_{\max}| + 5$, $y = 2j + 1$. Canonical content at §1.7 + archived VR §256.

The triple is **DERIVED** at canonical content; the question of whether the Diophantine identity holds geometrically (representation-theoretic content) is **D-A3-2** at §3.5 + CG §22.5 item D-A3-2.

### §6.2 Standing prohibitions

#### §6.2.1 Operational scope

Standing prohibitions are operational rules that derivation + verification work must not violate. They are distinct from F-flags (§4) — F-flags identify systematic failure modes that audit machinery flags at landing; standing prohibitions are **upstream** rules that prevent work from beginning in non-canonical directions in the first place. Both are operative across all dispatches; both are load-bearing throughout S64+ work.

Source: SESSION64_PROMPT §110–§124 "Standing prohibitions" block (consolidated from S58–S63 cumulative imprint).

#### §6.2.2 Standing prohibitions block

- **No LCDM-shaped vocabulary.** $H_0$, $R_{\rm Hubble}$, expansion, baryon loading, etc. are not valid inputs or framings; UDT is static (Theory Rule 5).
- **No SM / QED / QCD scaffolding imports without canonical grounding.** ΛCDM, Standard Model, quantum mechanics, QED, QCD may NOT appear in derivations. They may ONLY be used for comparing final UDT predictions against observations or standard-model values (Theory Rule 4).
- **Do not call the UDT metric "ansatz."** The metric is DERIVED at CG §1.0 (sympy-verified per S58-009); a consequence of GR + positional-dilation postulate under $T^t{}_t = T^r{}_r$ matter consistency + asymptotic flatness; Schwarzschild as unique vacuum limit.
- **Do not call canonical Form-T Dirac "ansatz."** Form-T is DERIVED at CG §4.4–§4.6 (canonical tetrad → Cartan spin-connection → coupled $G$, $F$ radial system + Geometric Neumann BC).
- **No linearization without explicit error bound.** Linearized backgrounds (e.g., $e^{-2\phi} \approx 1$, sinh ≈ argument) are invalid at project-relevant $\phi_0$ values. Always integrate the full nonlinear flux system; if an approximation is used, compute the error and flag it per archived VR §265 marker convention (§4.9).
- **No manuscript-framing of negative results.** Negative reconnaissance returns as **structural identification** of where the structure isn't, not as a story about something that "failed." Halt-don't-salvage; document the dead-end with operator-level localization.
- **Kaleidoscope Principle = observer-frame relativity only** (F119 narrow scope). The principle is the observation that what looks like distinct cosmological observables under different observer-frame projections are the static metric viewed through different geometric lenses. It is NOT a cross-dispatch pattern term for any other usage.
- **$\chi_{\rm matter} \neq \delta\phi_{\rm geom}$ upstream-scope discipline** (F121 + F128). Matter-sector $\chi$ perturbations are distinct from geometric $\phi$ perturbations; do not identify or conflate.
- **No "F129 pinning satisfied" claims at landing without explicit `# APPROXIMATION:` + `# SCAFFOLDING:` enumeration block in PONDER §-header** (archived VR §265 marker convention at §4.9). Strict-canonical pinning claims require both enumeration blocks empty.
- **F130 + F131 + F132 + F137 vigilance is load-bearing** at all φ-exponent derivation + verification work. PONDER §-headers must declare canonical-α vs composite-β target + enumerate structural decomposition (§4.5 + §4.6).
- **Phase 2 substantive derivation at forward-direction territory only** (S66-004 revision; superseded S65-004 + S64-005 framings per IH §49.10 §5.4). L1 DERIVED at (b)-type (S65-001); L3 + L2 STRUCTURAL-FINDING with closure pre-empted at canonical content (S65-003); L4 STRUCTURAL-FINDING (closure pre-empted at canonical content via four structurally independent reasons parallel to S65-003 + SE-9 amplification finding; S66-003). **Composite-matter Phase 2 forward arc at canonical content fully pre-empted.** Canonical-content extension territory (IH §49.10 §5.11) **singular substantive forward direction within composite-matter Phase 2 scope** (S66-004 promotion from parallel candidate; reconnaissance-grade preserved at substantive-charter level). Do not charter against parked sub-questions at §3.5 (D-PION-COEFF / D-PI-POWER-ORIGIN / V4-origin) or against archived VR §40.25 three-regime classification candidate. Closure via side-effect of substantive derivation work permitted; if a side-effect closure occurs, log without redirecting.
- **#29 cascade-confirmation discipline operative at every PONDER-landing audit.** Verifier disagreement is load-bearing signal, not rubber-stamp variation; verifiers should explicitly seek secondary errors (verdict-letter precision, convention discrepancies, completeness items) within agreement-with-primary outcomes.
- **κGF channel-matching at canonical CR-46 source per CG §8.5.4 lines 1091-1093 is an algebraic-identity restatement of the single canonical quantity $S \equiv T^r{}_r - T^t{}_t = -\Delta_{\rm Dirac}$, NOT a distinct-object coupling relation** (S65-003 STRUCTURAL-FINDING; S65-004 canonical-record-edit landing). **F129 caveat at the κGF-channel-matching layer DISSOLVED via substantive derivation** — the matching was not what the pre-S65-003 reading thought it was (suggestive coupling). The MF coupling-mediated closure mechanism is **pre-empted at canonical content** for three structurally independent reasons (per IH §49.10 §5.6 + active doc §3.2 D-COMP-MATTER-L3 row): CR-46 algebraic identity; canonical scalar EOM has no Dirac source at (b)-type partition per §8.5.1 line 1013; class-level rule-out via Branch-M §22.3.1 + Branch-C §12.12.20. The §255 violation reads as test-field anisotropy on metric-determined background at canonical content; not load-bearing for on-shell Einstein-equation closure. **F129 vigilance at other structural-closure claims remains operational** (e.g., L4 perturbation-tier work; canonical-content extension reconnaissance). **Future invocations of channel-matching at canonical-record content MUST engage the algebraic-identity-vs-coupling-relation distinction explicitly** — F138-7 candidate registered at active doc §4.10 (algebraic-identity-vs-coupling-relation pattern; informal-discipline tracking).
- **Cleanup arc COMPLETE at S63 close** — no further canonical-record-cleanup engagement at S64+ except where substantive derivation work surfaces dependency.
- **Path B (§25 full retirement) is BLOCKED on D-POLY-1 + D-SNE-PROJ-1 closures** (§3.4); deferred to later canonical-record-cleanup arc.
- **Preventive #29 charter-discipline pattern at charter sub-choice 1** carries forward to any dispatch with retirement-target-pinning or migration-target sub-choices. Explicit pinning prevents banner-phrase-literal-vs-intent ambiguity (F-candidate-S63-002-a at **NINETEEN-PRECEDENT** cumulative across S63 + S64 + S65 + S66 arc per active doc §4.10; promotion DEFERRED per Charles direction at S63 close, re-affirmed at S64 + S65 + S66 charter-locks).

- **F129 + F138 vigilance** load-bearing at all derivation work (§4.2 + §4.7).
- **F130 + F131 + F132 + F137 family** operational at all φ-exponent derivation + verification work (§4.3–§4.6).
